<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-onchocerciasis-river-blindness">3. ONCHOCERCIASIS (river blindness)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-onchocerciasis-river-blindness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Def: Onchocerciasis is an eye and skin disease caused by a worm (filaria) known as <em>Onchocerca volvulus</em>.</li>
<li>It is also called <em>River Blindness</em></li>
<li>It is transmitted to humans through exposure to repeated bites of infected <strong>blackfly</strong> called <em>Simulium damnosum</em></li>
<li>These blackflies breed in fast-flowing rivers and streams, mostly in remote villages located near fertile land where people rely on agriculture.</li>
<li>The disease manifests mainly as skin nodules on bony surfaces and causes eye lesions</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="life-cycle">Life cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#life-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Humans become infected when blackfly bites and deposit <em>Onchocerca</em> infective larvae into the skin.</li>
<li>Once inside the human body, the larvae mature into adults in around 3 months to 1 year.</li>
<li>The mature males and females then collect in balls, bound together by fibrous tissue which forms the typical nodule. The nodules are best seen on bony skin surfaces like elbow, shoulder scapula, skull, ribs and iliac crest</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Most adult female worms live in fibrous nodules under the skin and sometimes near muscles and joints</li>
<li>If a blackfly bites an infected person, onchocerciasis larvae can be ingested by the blackfly after which they migrate to the biting parts of the fly where they can be transmitted back to humans when it bites again.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-presentation">Clinical presentation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Has 3 different clinical presentation</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Skin nodules: Are caused by adult worms. Are firm and non tender ranging from 3mm to 3 cm in diameter.</li>
<li>Dermatitis: caused by presence of microfilariae in epidermis and manifests as itchy papules or macules. Later the skin become loose, scaly, atrophic and depigmented</li>
<li>River bindness: serious complication caused by presence of microfilariae in cornea and the anterior chamber of the eye. At first there is edema of the conjunctiva</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>small opaque spots on the cornea are formed. These spots are often accompanied by redness of the conjunctiva.</li>
<li>At a later stage, the cornea becomes permanently cloudy, which results in vision loss.</li>
<li>In infections that produce blindness, not only the cornea gets damaged but all anatomical parts of the eye are also affected, including the posterior part of the eye and the optic nerve.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The most common method of laboratory diagnosis used to identify microfilariae is a biopsy of the skin called a skin snip. Microfilariae emerge when the skin snip is placed in a saline solution.</li>
<li>Nodules can also be surgically removed to identify adult worms</li>
<li>A physical examination of the patient can detect localized dermatitis or subcutaneous nodules</li>
<li>NB: Onchocerca volvulus is not found in the blood therefore it cannot be used for diagnosis</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>First line treatment is ivermectin 150g/Kg orally either yearly or bi-annually.</li>
<li>Ivermectin kills circulating microfilariae as well as those that are still in adult female worms; this reduces the numbers of microfilariae in the skin and the production of new microfilariae by adult worms so the disease does not progress</li>
<li>Contra-indicated in pregnancy and breastfeeding women.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Six weeks course of doxycycline</li>
<li>Diethylcarbamazine {Hetrazan or Banocide</li>
<li>Kills microfilariae though it has no effect on adult worm</li>
<li>Surgical excision when nodules are located in the head</li>
<li>MAIN GOAL OF THERAPY: to prevent development of irreversible lesions and alleviate symptoms</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Community based administration of ivermectin every 6-12 months</li>
<li>Vector control: usually ground larviciding using environmentally safe insecticides in breeding places</li>
<li>Personal protection measures against biting insects. wearing long sleeves and trousers during the day when blackflies bite, and wearing permethrin- treated clothing</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="summary">summary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Onchocerciasis, commonly known as river blindness, is caused by the parasitic worm <em>Onchocerca volvulus</em>.</li>
<li>It is transmitted to humans through exposure to repeated bites of infected blackflies of the genus <em>Simulium</em>.</li>
<li>Symptoms include severe itching, disfiguring skin conditions and visual impairment, including permanent blindness</li>
<li>Community-directed treatment with ivermectin is the core strategy to eliminate onchocerciasis in Africa. In the Americas the strategy is biannual large-scale treatment with ivermectin</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="schistosomiasis">SCHISTOSOMIASIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#schistosomiasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS 0002</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction-to-schistosomiasis">Introduction to Schistosomiasis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction-to-schistosomiasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Schistosomiasis, also known as bilharzia or snail fever, is a parasitic disease carried by fresh water snails infected with one of the five varieties of the parasite Schistosoma.</li>
<li>Can contract it swimming in lakes, ponds and other bodies of water infested with the parasites snail host</li>
<li>Causative organisms</li>
<li>S. mansoni</li>
<li>S. haematobium</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="snail-hosts">Snail hosts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#snail-hosts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The different species of <em>Schistosoma</em> have different types of snails serving as their intermediate hosts; these hosts are:</li>
<li><em>Biomphalaria for S mansoni</em></li>
<li><em>Oncomelania for S japonicum</em></li>
<li><em>Bulinus for S haematobium</em> and <em>S intercalatum</em></li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="risk-factors">Risk factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Contact with freshwater sources where infected snails carrying the disease live</li>
<li>Children under age 14</li>
<li>Individuals with labor or domestic chores centered around freshwater areas</li>
<li>Swimming, bathing, fishing and even domestic chores such as laundry and herding livestock can put people at risk of contracting the disease.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="transmission">Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Schistosomiasis is transmitted by contact with contaminated fresh water (lakes and ponds, rivers, dams) inhabited by snails carrying the parasite</li>
<li>Larvae emerge from the snails and swim in the water until they come into contact with an individual and penetrate the skin.</li>
<li>The larvae migrate to the blood vessels where they mate and produce eggs. Some eggs travel to the bladder or intestines and are passed into the urine or stool. Others remain trapped in the body and cause damage to internal organs..</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="life-cycle">Life Cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#life-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>(Eggs  larvae  into snail)</p>
<ol>
<li>Parasite eggs are released into freshwater (from human urine, feces)</li>
<li>Eggs hatch into <em>miracidia</em>, free swimming larvae</li>
<li>Miracidia find &amp; infect snail host</li>
<li>In the snail miracidia develop into many free swimming forms called <em>cercariae</em> within 4-6 weeks of entering snail. THEY ARE INFECTIVE AGENTS OF SCHISTOSOMIASIS</li>
<li>Cercariae are shed from the snail 4-7 weeks</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="kenya-medical-training-college">KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kenya-medical-training-college" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<p>cont</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>They can live up to 48 hrs unless they infect human beings. Human become infected when they enter cercarie infected water while bathing, playing, laundering, cultivating or fishing.</li>
<li>The cercarie penetrate skin, enter the blood stream, and are carried to the liver or bladder where they develop into adult worm</li>
</ol>
<p>NB: DRAW THE DIAGRAM SHOWING THE LIFE CYCLE OF SCHISTOSOMIASIS</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="distinguishing-between-s-haematobium-and-s-mansoni">Distinguishing between S.haematobium and S.mansoni<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#distinguishing-between-s-haematobium-and-s-mansoni" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Adult worm reside in venous plexus of bladder</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Eggs are excreted with urine</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vector snail is Bulinus which is found in temporary water bodies such as ponds</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Presents with hematuria in early stages</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reside in mesenteric veins of the bowel</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Eggs are excreted with feaces</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vector snail is Biomphalaria found in permanent water bodies such as lakes, rivers dams</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Presents with bloody diarrhoea" mansoni dysentry in early stages</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disease-development">Disease development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disease-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Schostosomiasis has several stages of development in the body.</li>
<li>The development include Invasion, maturation, established infection and late stage</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-invasion">1. Invasion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-invasion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Cercarie penetrate into the skin. This causes cercarial dermatitis with itching papules and local edema.</li>
<li>The cercarie then enter the circulation and reach the liver via right side of the heart and lungs</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-maturation">2. Maturation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-maturation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Schistosomes mature in the liver.</li>
<li>The stage presents with:</li>
<li> Fever</li>
<li> Eosinophilis</li>
<li> Abdominal pain</li>
<li> Transient generalised urticaria. It is also known as Katayana syndrome</li>
<li>After maturation, the adult worm descend into the portal vein.</li>
<li>S. mansoni migrate to the mesentric veins in the intestinal wall and S. haematobium finds its way to the venous plexus of the bladder</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-established-infection">3. Established infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-established-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Is the stage of egg production</li>
<li>Eggs are produced by female in small veins of the bowel or bladder.</li>
<li>Some eggs penetrate tissues and other do not. They remain in blood and are carried to the liver and lungs.</li>
<li>The eggs which do not reach lumen provoke inflammatory reaction and formation of granulomas. A granuloma is a small area of inflammation in tissue</li>
<li>These inflammatory reaction causes bloody diarrhoea and cramps in, S.mansoni and Terminal haematuria and dysuria in S.haematobium</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="late-stage">Late stage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#late-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Late stage is characterized by fibrosis and calcification which occur when there are many eggs in the tissues.</li>
<li>Fibrosis refers to the thickening and scarring of connective tissue, usually as a result of injury.</li>
<li>Calcification is the process in which calcium builds up in body tissue where there normally isn't any calcium. Over time, the buildup can harden and disrupt your body's normal processes.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="late-stage-in-the-bladder">Late stage in the bladder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#late-stage-in-the-bladder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Late stage around the bladder results in:</li>
<li> Obstruction and dilatation of ureters and hydronephrosis possibly leading to kidney failure</li>
<li> Pyelonephritis</li>
<li> Calcification of the bladder which shows on x-ray or ultrasound investigation</li>
<li> Cancer of the bladder</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="late-stage-in-the-liver-and-lungs">Late stage in the liver and lungs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#late-stage-in-the-liver-and-lungs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Late stage in the liver leads to: portal hypertension, splenomegaly, anemia, oesophageal varices and massive bleeding</li>
<li>In the lungs, fibrosis leads to pulmonary hypertension which leads to congestive heart failure</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="acute-and-chronic-infection">Acute and chronic infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acute-and-chronic-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="acute-infection">ACUTE INFECTION:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acute-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Occur when Cercariae penetrate skin  rash</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>called <strong>schistosome</strong> or <strong>swimmers itch develop</strong>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Eggs laid in target organs release antigens which cause Katayama fever characterised by:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>fever</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>urticaria</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>malaise</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>diarrhea</p>
</li>
</ul>

Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCERG</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chronic-infection">Chronic infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chronic-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms of chronic infection caused by eggs that travel to various parts of body</li>
<li>Eggs remain trapped in host tissues  granulomatous inflammatory immune response</li>
<li>Granulomas: macrophages surrounded by lymphocytes</li>
<li>Fibrosis develop in the late stages</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="symptoms">Symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Symptoms for the disease vary depending on the type of worm involved and the location of the parasite inside the body:</p>
<p>&gt; initial itching and rash at infection site ("swimmer's itch")</p>
<ul>
<li>The classic sign of urogenital schistosomiasis is haematuria (blood in urine)</li>
<li>Abdominal pain and bloody diarrhea</li>
<li>Anemia</li>
<li>Fever, chills and muscle aches</li>
<li>Inflammation and scarring of the bladder</li>
<li>Lymph node enlargement</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="microscopic-detection">Microscopic Detection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#microscopic-detection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Take stool or urine sample to detect eggs</li>
<li><em>S. haematobium</em> eggs are oval and have a spike at the tip</li>
<li><em>S. mansoni</em> eggs have a spike on the side (spine)</li>
<li>If they are repeatedly negative, a rectal or bowel biopsy can be done</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Praziquantel {biltricide} is the drug of choice for all schistosomal species</li>
<li>Single dose of 40mg/kg is effective in S.haematobium and S. mansoni</li>
<li>For patients with heavy infections{over 800 eggs per gramme of stool}, a total dose of 60mg/kg in two equally divided doses 4-6 hrs apart.</li>
<li>Drug is best administered after food and in the evening</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="con">con<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#con" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Oxamniquine {vansil} is effective only against S.mansoni.</li>
<li>The drug is used in all stages of infection</li>
<li>Dose varies with the geographical origin of S.mansoni between 30mg/kg to 60mg/kg.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS 001</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-and-control-of-schistosomiasis">Prevention and control of schistosomiasis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control-of-schistosomiasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Avoiding contact with water known to contain cercariae by:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Providing safe water supply to the community.</li>
<li>Construct footbridges across infested rivers and streams.</li>
<li>Providing safe recreational bathing sites</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<p>cont</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Preventing water becoming contaminated with eggs by:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Health information on safe excreta disposal</li>
<li>Treating infected persons</li>
<li>Providing sanitary facilities</li>
<li>Protecting water supplies from fecal pollution by animal reservoir hosts</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol start="3">
<li>Minimizing the risk of infection from new water conservation, irrigation schemes and hydroelectric power development by:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Constructing settlement camps away from canal drains and irrigation canals and providing latrines and sufficient safe water for domestic use.</li>
<li>Lining canals with cement and keeping them free from silt and vegetation in which snails can breed</li>
<li>Filling in formerly used irrigation ditches with clean soil to bury snail hosts.</li>
<li>Varying the water levels in the system</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol start="4">
<li>Destroying snail intermediate hosts, mainly by:
 Using molluscides where this is affordable, feasible and will not harm important animal and plant life.
 Removing vegetation from locally used water places, draining swamps and other measures to eradicate snail habitats.
 Taking environmental measures to prevent seasonal flooding which results in an increase in snail numbers in transmission.
 Biological means by introducing predators like fish and insects that eat snails and Marisa cornuarieties snail that competes with intermediate host of schistosomiasis.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="kenya-medical-training-college">KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kenya-medical-training-college" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol start="5">
<li>Treating water supplies by:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Using a chlorine disinfectant where possible</li>
<li>Storing water for 48 hours to allow time for any cercariae to die.</li>
<li>Using filter systems at water inputs to prevent cercariae from entering</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol start="6">
<li>Mass or selective chemotherapy In areas with high morbidity and intensity of infection:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>chemotherapy can be given by health center staff in the community/ school to reduce morbidity.</li>
<li>Community health workers can play key role in community mobilization and evaluation of treatment.</li>
<li>With the introduction of new drugs such as praziquantel mass treatment has been possible in Kenya</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Complications of schistosomiasis include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Gastrointestinal (GI) bleeding</li>
<li>GI obstruction</li>
<li>Malnutrition</li>
<li>Schistosomal nephropathy</li>
<li>Renal failure</li>
<li>Pyelonephritis</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<p>YELLOW FEVER</p>
<p>OVERVIEW OF KENYAN SITUATION</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="kenyan-situation">KENYAN SITUATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kenyan-situation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Between 15 and 18 March 2016, the National IHR Focal Point of Kenya notified WHO of 2 imported cases of yellow fever (YF).</li>
<li>Both cases were male Kenyan nationals, in their early 30s, working in Luanda, Angola. Both travelled while symptomatic and none were vaccinated against yellow fever prior to traveling to Angola.</li>
<li>The first case developed symptoms on 8 March in Luanda and travelled to Kenya on 12 March. At his arrival, he was hospitalized in a private clinic in Nairobi and was later referred to another health care facility. The patient died after experiencing multi-organ failure.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The second case presented symptoms on 1 March in Luanda, and flew back to Kenya on 7 March. He went to his home town (Namanga) on the Kenyan-Tanzanian Border. He returned to Nairobi to seek treatment on 11 March where he was hospitalised. The patient was treated and has since recovered and been discharged.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="what-is-yellow-fever">What is yellow fever<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-yellow-fever" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Yellow fever is an acute viral disease transmitted by infected mosquitoes.</li>
<li>It is caused by <strong>yellow fever virus</strong></li>
<li>The "yellow" in the name refers to the jaundice that affects some patients.</li>
<li>It is characterised by sudden onset of fever, rigors, headache, jaundice, muscle pain, nausea and vomiting.</li>
<li>It is a zoonotic disease of forest monkeys</li>
<li>It is transmitted by a mosquito vector called <strong>Aedes aegypty</strong></li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="transmission">TRANSMISSION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Yellow fever virus has three transmission cycles: jungle (sylvatic), intermediate (savannah), and urban.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The jungle (sylvatic) cycle involves transmission of the virus between non-human primates (e.g., monkeys) and mosquito species found in the forest canopy. The virus is transmitted by mosquitoes from monkeys to humans when humans are visiting or working in the jungle.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In Africa, an intermediate (savannah) cycle exists that involves transmission of virus from mosquitoes to humans living or working in jungle border areas. In this cycle, the virus can be transmitted from monkey to human or from human to human via mosquitoes.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>The urban cycle involves transmission of the virus between humans and urban mosquitoes, primarily <em>Aedes aegypti</em>. The virus is usually brought to the urban setting by a viremic human who was infected in the jungle or savannah</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="signs-and-symptoms">Signs and symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Once contracted, the yellow fever virus incubates in the body for 3 to 6 days.</li>
<li>The most common Symptoms are fever, muscle pain with prominent backache, headache, loss of appetite, and nausea or vomiting. In most cases, symptoms disappear after 3 to 4 days.</li>
<li>A small percentage of patients, however, enter a second, more toxic phase within 24 hours of recovering from initial symptoms</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>High fever returns and several body systems are affected,</li>
<li>usually the liver and the kidneys. In this phase people are develop and abdominal pain with vomiting.</li>
<li>Bleeding can occur from the mouth, nose, eyes or stomach. Half of the patients who enter the toxic phase die within 7 - 10 days.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A presumptive diagnosis of yellow fever is often based on the patient's clinical features, places and dates of travel (if the patient is from a non-endemic country or area), activities, and epidemiologic history of the location where the presumed infection occurred</li>
<li>Laboratory diagnosis of yellow fever is generally accomplished by testing of serum to detect virus-specific IgM and neutralizing antibodies. Sometimes the virus can be found in blood samples taken early in the illness.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="differential-diagnosis">Differential diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#differential-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Viral hepatitis</li>
<li>Malaria</li>
<li>Leptospirosis</li>
<li>Relapsing fever</li>
<li>ebola</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment">TREATMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Treatment is directed at symptomatic relief or life-saving interventions. Rest, fluids, and use of analgesics and antipyretics may relieve symptoms of fever and aching</li>
<li>There is currently no specific anti-viral drug for yellow fever but specific care to treat dehydration, liver and kidney failure, and fever improves outcomes. Associated bacterial infections can be treated with antibiotics.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-and-control-measures">Prevention and control measures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control-measures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Immunization against yellow fever in regional hospitals, international airports and border entry points</li>
<li>Isolating all contacts in screened quarters to prevent spread of infection</li>
<li>Disease notification of all suspected cases</li>
<li>Mass immunisation campaigns to cover all surrounding areas infected with aedes mosquito</li>
<li>urging all county health departments and relevant stakeholders to enhance disease surveillance, in particular for yellow fever, at points of entry (PoEs) and within the country</li>
<li>providing information to travellers on yellow fever vaccination and implementation of inspection of yellow fever certificates at PoEs.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="kenya-medical-training-college">KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kenya-medical-training-college" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-yellow-fever-outbreak">MANAGEMENT OF YELLOW FEVER OUTBREAK<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-yellow-fever-outbreak" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Notify the health authorities of all suspected cases</li>
<li>Verify the presence of outbreak by checking medical and laboratory records in health facilities</li>
<li>Isolating all contacts in screened quarters to prevent spread of infection</li>
<li>Mass immunisation campaigns to cover all surrounding areas infected with aedes mosquito</li>
<li>Carrying out social mobilization activities;</li>
<li>Activating a national task force to manage the detected imported cases;</li>
<li>Strengthening the testing capability of the reference laboratory</li>
<li>providing information to travellers on yellow fever vaccination and implementation of inspection of yellow fever certificates at PoEs</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="leishmaniasis">LEISHMANIASIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#leishmaniasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Leishmaniasis is a parasitic disease caused by the <em>Leishmania</em> parasite.</li>
<li>The vector that transmit leishmaniasis is sand flies {Phlepotomus spp.</li>
<li>The disease is contracted from a bite from an infected sand fly</li>
<li>The disease is transmitted from animals to humans and humans to humans</li>
<li>There are two forms of leishmaniasis in Africa. Visceral and Cutaneous leishmaniasis</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="major-risk-factors">Major risk factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#major-risk-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Socioeconomic conditions
Poverty increases the risk for leishmaniasis. Poor housing and domestic sanitary conditions (such as a lack of waste management or open sewerage) may increase sandfly breeding and resting sites, as well as their access to humans. Sandflies are attracted to crowded housing as these provide a good source of blood-meals. Human behaviour, such as sleeping outside or on the ground, may increase risk. The use of insecticide-treated bednets reduces risk.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Malnutrition
Diets lacking protein-energy, iron, vitamin A and zinc increase the risk that an infection will progress to kala-azar.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-population-mobility">3. Population mobility<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-population-mobility" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Epidemics of both cutaneous and visceral leishmaniasis are often associated with migration and the movement of non-immune people into areas with existing transmission cycles. Occupational exposure as well as widespread deforestation remain important factors. For example, people settling in areas that used to be forests may be moving near sandflies habitat. This can lead to a rapid increase in cases.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-environmental-changes">4. Environmental changes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-environmental-changes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Environmental changes that can affect the incidence of leishmaniasis include urbanization, domestication of the transmission cycle and the incursion of agricultural farms and settlements into forested areas</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<p>cont</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Climate change</li>
</ol>
<p>Leishmaniasis is climate-sensitive, and strongly affected by changes in rainfall, temperature and humidity.</p>
<ul>
<li>changes in temperature, rainfall and humidity can have strong effects on vectors and reservoir hosts by altering their distribution and influencing their survival and population sizes;</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="visceral-leishmaniasis-kala-azar">Visceral Leishmaniasis{Kala-azar}<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#visceral-leishmaniasis-kala-azar" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Visceral leishmaniasis is sometimes known as systemic leishmaniasis.</li>
<li>It usually occurs two to eight months after being bitten by a sand fly.</li>
<li>Is spread by sandfly <em>Phlepotomus Orientalis</em> in sudan and <em>Phlepotomus martini</em> in kenya</li>
<li>It is a chronic disease of reticuloendothelial system.</li>
<li>reticuloendothelial system is a network of phagocytic cells and tissues found throughout the body, especially in the blood, general connective tissue, spleen, liver, lungs, bone marrow, and lymph nodes</li>
<li>Found in west pokot, Rift valley, Tana and Athi Rivers.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features-of-visceral-leishmaniasis">Clinical features of visceral leishmaniasis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features-of-visceral-leishmaniasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Fever that lasts for weeks or months</li>
<li>Chills</li>
<li>Anemia</li>
<li>Weight loss</li>
<li>Splenomegaly</li>
<li>Weakness</li>
<li>Cough</li>
<li>Enlarged liver</li>
<li>Decreased production of red blood cells (rbcs)</li>
<li>Bleeding</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="development-of-visceral-leishmaniasis">Development of visceral leishmaniasis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#development-of-visceral-leishmaniasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Incubation period is 4-10 months</li>
<li>Definitive symptoms begin with papular skin lesion called leishmanioma</li>
<li>The disease may set in gradually or suddenly</li>
<li>Sudden onset presents with intermittent fever which last 2-6 weeks before becoming persistent</li>
<li>Gradual onset starts with discomfort in the left hypocondrium as the skin enlarges and it can run up to 1-2 years</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Stained slides or cultures of a tissue aspirate or biopsy specimen of spleen, liver, bone marrow or lymp node.</li>
<li>Diagnostic yield is highest for splenic aspiration.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Sodium stibogluconate or meglumine antimonate): is a drug of choice Used in Viceral leishmaniasis; It is given as IV or IM in doses of 0.1 to 0.2ml/kg{1ml=100mg} daily for 6-30 days.</li>
<li>Pentamidine Isothianate may be given IM in doses of 1.1ml/kg{1ml=40mg} 3 times weekly until 10 doses have been administered</li>
<li>Amphotericin B preserved for cases resistant to other drugs. Given by slow IV infusion in 5% dextrose in doses of 1mg/kg on alternate days until a total of 2g has been given</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Miltefosine is highly effective oral agent. Given at a dosage of 50 to 100 mg daily for 28 days</li>
<li>Paromomycin an aminoglycoside is used as an adjunct therapy to stibogluconate.</li>
<li>Complete bed rest</li>
<li>Supply of adequate nutrition</li>
<li>Correction of anemia</li>
<li>Treatment of intercurrent infections</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cutaneous-leishmaniasis">Cutaneous Leishmaniasis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cutaneous-leishmaniasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Also known as oriental sore</li>
<li>Is characterized by single or several chronic cutaneous sores which usually heal spontaneously</li>
<li>Caused by leishmania aethiopa in Kenya and Leishmania tropica major in west Africa</li>
<li>Zoonotic reservoirs are dogs</li>
<li>The vectors are Phlepotomus papatsi and Phebotomus sergenti</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-presentation">Clinical presentation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Incubation period is 2-8 weeks</li>
<li>The disease starts as a small papule on the face which expands and grows over several weeks to form a single ulcer or multiple ulcers</li>
<li>When the lesion infiltrate the skin diffusely, it may present like leprosy</li>
<li>There may be lymphadenopathy</li>
<li>Spontaneous healing starts 2- months later hence, there is no need for treatment</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="key-strategies-for-prevention-and-control">Key strategies for prevention and control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#key-strategies-for-prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Early diagnosis and effective case management: reduces the prevalence of the disease and prevents disabilities and death. Currently there are highly effective and safe anti-leishmanial medicines particularly for visceral leishmaniasis.</li>
<li>Vector control: helps to reduce or interrupt transmission of disease by controlling sandflies, especially in domestic conditions. Control methods include insecticide spray, use of insecticide-treated nets, environmental management and personal protection.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS 001</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Effective disease surveillance: Early detection and treatment of cases helps to reduce transmission and to monitor the spread and burden of disease.</li>
<li>Control of animal reservoir hosts.</li>
<li>Social mobilization and strengthening partnerships  mobilization and education of the community with effective behavioural change interventions must always use locally tailored communication strategies.</li>
<li>Partnership and collaboration with various stakeholders and other vector-borne disease control programmes is critical.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="kenya-medical-training-college">KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kenya-medical-training-college" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
