<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dracunculosis">DRACUNCULOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dracunculosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Dracunculiasis (commonly known as guinea-worm disease) is a parasitic disease caused by <em>Dracunculus medinensis</em> - a long, thread-like worm.</li>
<li>It is transmitted exclusively when people drink stagnant water contaminated with parasite-infected water-fleas (<em>Cyclops</em>).</li>
<li>From the time infection occurs, it takes between 1014 months for the transmission cycle to complete until a mature worm emerges from the body.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="transmission-and-life-cycle">Transmission and life cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#transmission-and-life-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It is transmitted by drinking water containing water fleas (<em>Cyclops</em> species) that have ingested <em>Dracunculus</em> larvae.</li>
<li>In the human body, the larvae are released and migrate through the intestinal wall into body tissues, where they develop into adult worms.</li>
<li>The female worms move through the person's subcutaneous tissue, causing intense pain, and eventually emerge through the skin, usually at the feet, producing oedema, a blister and eventually an ulcer, accompanied by fever, nausea, and vomiting.</li>
<li>If they come into contact with water as they are emerging, the female worms discharge their larvae, setting in motion a new life cycle.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-picture">Clinical picture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-picture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>An itching and painful blister develops at the site where the adult female worm emerges thus forming an ulcer</li>
<li>Ulcers are very common in body areas which are most likely to come in contact with water e.g feet and genitals. The thread-like worm can be seen in ulcer</li>
<li>After discharging larvae for 2-3 weeks, the female worm dies and is extruded or absorbed</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Other Symptoms include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Pain in joints</li>
<li>Nausea,</li>
<li>Fever</li>
<li>Pruritus</li>
<li>Blisters</li>
<li>Ulcers</li>
<li>Eosinophilia</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Gradual extraction of the worm by winding of a few centimetres on a stick each day</li>
<li>Surgical excision</li>
<li>Metronidazole 250mg TDS for 10 days relieve symptoms but no activity against worm</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Heightening surveillance to detect every case within 24 hours of worm emergence;</li>
<li>Preventing transmission from each worm by treatment, cleaning and bandaging regularly the affected skin-area until the worm is completely expelled from the body;</li>
<li>Preventing drinking water contamination by advising the patient to avoid wading into water;</li>
<li>Ensuring wider access to improved drinking-water supplies to prevent infection;</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">Cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Filtering water and boiling water from open water bodies before drinking;</li>
<li>Implementing vector control by using the larvicide temephos;</li>
<li>Promoting health education and behaviour change</li>
</ul>

<p>B.DISEASES CAUSED BY FECAL CONTAMINATION</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">INTRODUCTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Causative organisms of the diseases in this group are excreted in the stools of infected persons</li>
<li>The portal of entry for these organism is mouth</li>
<li>Organisms have to pass through environment from feaces of infected person to GI of a susceptible person</li>
<li>This is called fecal-Oral transmission route</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-cholera">1. CHOLERA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-cholera" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Cholera is an acute intestinal disease characterised by sudden onset of profuse watery stool, vomiting, rapid dehydration and circulatory collapse</li>
<li>Causative organism: Vibrio cholerae</li>
<li>Vibrios are Gram-negative, highly motile curved rods with a single polar flagellum</li>
<li>They tolerate alkaline media that kill most intestinal commensals, but they are sensitive to acid.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="vibrio-species">Vibrio species<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vibrio-species" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>There are over 100 vibrio species known but only the "cholerae" species are responsible for cholera epidemics</li>
<li>
<ol>
<li>Vibrio cholerae species: are divided into 2 serogroups:</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>Vibrio cholerae O1, subdivided into Classical and El Tor biotypes,</li>
<li>
<ol start="2">
<li>Vibrio cholerae O139 serogroup.</li>
</ol>
</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
ICER</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="risk-factors">RISK FACTORS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Overcrowding (internally displaced people, refugee, camps, population gathering)</li>
<li>Etc)</li>
<li>Inadequate quantity and/or quality of water</li>
<li>Inadequate personal hygiene</li>
<li>Poor washing facilities</li>
<li>Inappropriate or poor sanitation</li>
<li>Inadequate food safety</li>
<li>Inappropriate funeral services for cholera victims</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cholera-transmission">Cholera transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cholera-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Transmission occurs from man to man via Fecally Contaminated Water Fruits &amp; Vegetables</li>
<li>Uncontrolled water sources such as wells, lakes, ponds, streams and rivers pose a great threat.</li>
<li>Contaminated Food Drinks: Ingestion of contaminated food and drinks have been associated with outbreaks of cholera.</li>
<li>Bottle feeding could be a significant risk factor for infants.</li>
<li>Fruits and vegetables washed with contaminated water can be a source of infection. After preparation, cooked food may be contaminated through contaminated hands and/or flies.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathogenesis">Pathogenesis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathogenesis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The large majority of ingested bacteria are destroyed by stomach acidity; surviving bacteria colonize intestinal cells, where they multiply and produce a very powerful enterotoxin that causes profuse watery diarrhea by a secretion mechanism</li>
<li>The toxin adheres to intestinal cells and causes an excretion of isotonic fluid in the intestinal lumen</li>
<li>it is the enterotoxin that causes fluid loss and diarrhea</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="host-defenses">Host Defenses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#host-defenses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Gastric acid, mucus secretion, and intestinal motility are the prime nonspecific defenses against <em>V cholerae</em>.</li>
<li>Breastfeeding in endemic areas is important in protecting infants from disease.</li>
<li>Disease results in effective specific immunity, involving primarily secretory immunoglobulin (IgA), as well as IgG antibodies, against vibrios, enterotoxin and other products.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-picture">Clinical picture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-picture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Incubation period is 2-3 days</li>
<li>Develop in 3 stages</li>
</ul>
<p> First Stage :</p>
<ul>
<li> There is passage of profuse watery stool. The watery stool has classical rice water appearance</li>
<li> The patient starts vomiting</li>
<li> Severe cramps in the abdomen and limps develops from loss of salts</li>
</ul>
<p> Second stage</p>
<ul>
<li> Collapse from dehydration: the body is cold, skin is dry and inelastic. The pulses are rapid and feeble with low Bp or hypotension</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">Cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Third stage</li>
<li> Disease recover spontaneously or with treatment.</li>
<li> Diarrhea decreases and the patient is able to take treatment</li>
</ul>
<p>The typical presentation of cholera</p>
<p>sudden onset of profuse painless watery stools, sometimes rice water like, often accompanied by vomiting. There is no fever. Dehydration appears within 12 to 24 hours</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-cholera-outbreak">Management of Cholera outbreak<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-cholera-outbreak" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Notify the sub county or county medical officer</li>
<li>Admit the patients on temporary hospitals {school or a church} or cholera treatment centres.</li>
<li>Isolate the patients to prevent transmission</li>
<li>Do not refer suspected cases. Increases the risk of transmission</li>
<li>Take stool specimens for culture to the national laboratory for confirmation</li>
<li>Prepare large amounts of rehydration fluid</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Rehydrate patients with oral fluids to prevent hypovolemic shock</li>
<li>Administer intravenous fluids for patients with shock only for a short time</li>
<li>Monitor the patient frequently, and reassess their hydration status at intervals.</li>
<li>Treat patients with cholera beds with central hole through which continuous stools can pass into the bucket and measured</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Dispose the vomitus or stools in pit latrine or a septic tank</li>
<li>Clean the Hospital equipments with disinfectant such as 5% lysol</li>
<li>Administer tetracycline 2g as a single dose or doxycycline 300mg as a single dose. Other alternatives include Erithromycin 40mg/kg daily in 3 divided doses for 3 days. Ciprofloxacin can be given as a single dose of 30mg/kg for patients resistance to tetracycline</li>
<li>Cotrimoxazole 960mg BD can be given for 3 days in adult</li>
<li>Give health education to the community on how cholera is spread and to make water safe for drinking and handling of food</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-and-control-measures">Prevention and control measures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control-measures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Surveillance: continuous monitoring of all aspects of disease including collection of morbidity and mortality reports, field investigations of epidemics or individual cases and laboratory investigations</li>
<li>Proper and timely case management in cholera treatment centres</li>
<li>Water purification: All water used for drinking, washing, or cooking should be sterilized by either boiling, chlorination safe excreta disposal</li>
<li>Proper waste disposal including construction of pit latrines in the community and maintaining cleanliness</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hand washing and personal hygiene: Wash hands often with soap and safe water. If no soap: scrub hands with ash or sand and rinse with safe water.</li>
<li>Food safety: wash with safe water. Cook food well, keep it covered. Left overs should be protected against contamination. Food preparation, storage and service area should always be kept clean.</li>
<li>Inspection of market places to ensure they maintain hygienic standards.</li>
<li>Health education aims at communities adopting preventive behaviour for averting contamination.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Food handlers should wear a clean gown and apron/hair cover when preparing and serving food; gowns used during food preparation and service should be removed when visiting toilet, cleaning rooms and during compound sanitation</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="giardiasis">GIARDIASIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#giardiasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This is an infection of the small intestines by protozoa called <em>Giardia lamblia</em>.</li>
<li>The disease may be mild (asymptomatic) in some individuals, while in others it may cause diarrhoea, malabsorption of digested nutrients and weight loss.</li>
<li>Giardiasis is found in all the countries of the world, but it is more common in developing countries such as Kenya, where the water supply may be contaminated by human faeces or sewerage.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mode-of-transmission">Mode of Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mode-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Often, the disease is spread from person to person, especially within families by asymptomatic carriers.</li>
<li>Cysts which are excreted in the stool of an infected person remain infectious for up to three months in cold water or four days if the temperature is 37C.</li>
<li>As soon as the cysts are ingested by a human being, they are activated by the hydrochloric acid in the stomach.</li>
<li>Trophozoites emerge and adhere to the wall of the upper portion of the small intestine. Here they begin to multiply and in about 10 - 14 days, the symptoms manifest</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features">Clinical features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Acute giardiasis is characterised by sudden onset of nausea, loss of appetite, abdominal distension (bloating sensation), prominent bowel sounds, and diarrhoea with frequent, frothy, yellowish stools with offensive odour. Fatigue, lethargy and weight loss often occur.</li>
<li>After about three weeks the symptoms reduce in severity and for many of the patients, this is the beginning of spontaneous recovery.</li>
<li>Some patients however, remain symptomatic and continue to lose weight because of ongoing malabsorption of nutrients, mostly fat, vitamin B12 and lactose. The disease may persist for months or years</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Diagnosis of giardiasis is often difficult to establish because stool examination rarely reveals motile trophozoites. However, approximately 60% of samples will show cysts.</li>
<li>The diagnosis is therefore made through the following ways:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Stool microscopy to show cysts (three separate stool specimens should be collected to increase sensitivity of the test)</li>
<li>Serology (giardia antigens can be detected in stools) - immunological test</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS 001</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Oral tinidazole 50mg/kg body weight single dose</li>
<li>Oral metronidazole 2g single dose. Repeat the dose after ten days to increase the cure rate</li>
<li>Oral metronidazole 250mg eight hourly for seven days</li>
<li>Quinacrine (Atabrine)</li>
<li>Dose 100mg tid x 5 to 7 days (7 mg / kg / day)</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The cysts of giardia lamblia are not affected by chlorine treatment of water or by iodine. However, they are highly susceptible to heat, therefore, the following preventive measures are important:</li>
</ul>
<p>a) Cooking food and boiling drinking water to kill the cysts
b) Advise people to avoid eating raw salads, ice cream, unpeeled fruit and ice cubes in endemic areas
c) Use of sand filters is also effective in protecting water from giardia cysts
d) Tracing and treatment of healthy human carriers</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="amoebiasis">AMOEBIASIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#amoebiasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This is a protozoal infection mainly of the intestinal mucous membrane in humans caused by <em>entamoeba histolytica</em>.</li>
<li>The disease is found in all parts of the world but more common where sanitary conditions are poor.</li>
<li>Amoebiasis can occur in families or spread through institutions but usually does not occur in epidemics</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mode-of-transmission">Mode of Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mode-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Cysts are passed from person to person by the faecal-oral route, by fingers soiled with faeces either directly into the mouth or via food.</li>
<li>Infections may also occur from drinking contaminated water.</li>
<li>Amoebiasis can occasionally spread from the bowels to other organs of the body, especially to the liver leading to amoebic liver disease</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features">Clinical features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The signs and symptoms of amoebiasis include:
a) Colicky abdominal pain
b) Watery foul smelling diarrhoea containing blood-streaked mucus
c) There may be a hard large tender abdominal mass (amoebic)</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathogenesis">Pathogenesis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathogenesis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Once the cysts are ingested, the emerging trophozoites take up residence in the intestinal mucosa.</li>
<li>The organisms multiply in the mucosa (causing the formation of bottle-shaped ulcers each 1-2cm in diameter).</li>
<li>Too many such ulcers may cover the large intestine. Some of the ulcers may become perforated leading to severe peritonitis with shock.</li>
<li>In the small intestines, the entamoeba histolytica may pass through the mucous membrane and enter the liver. After a variable incubation period a liver abscess may form.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This is reached by doing a stool microscopy for cysts of <em>entamoeba histolytica</em>.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>No treatment is necessary for asymptomatic patients as in time they clear the infection.</li>
<li>However, for invasive disease either one of the following treatments is effective:</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<li>Oral metronidazole 800mg eight hourly for five to seven days</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="extra-intestinal-amoebic-disease">Extra-intestinal Amoebic Disease<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#extra-intestinal-amoebic-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The most common site for extra-intestinal amoebiasis is the liver where it forms a liver abscess.</li>
<li>Other secondary sites include lungs and skin leading to:
a) Amoebic infection of the skin
b) Amoebic balanitis : inflammation of penis caused by E. hystolytica
c) Amoebic lung abscess
d) Amoebic brain abscess</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>cysts-passers who are usually asymptomatic are responsible for the spread of amoebic dysentery</li>
<li>Therefore in order to prevent and control this disease, you need to do the following:</li>
<li>Advise people to boil drinking water (chlorination does not kill the cysts)</li>
<li>Search for and treat carriers among food handlers</li>
<li>Commence a campaign for more latrines in an area with endemic amoebiasis</li>
<li>Conduct community campaigns about good personal hygiene practices, such as regular hand washing</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hepatitis">HEPATITIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hepatitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hepatitis is an inflammation of the liver.</li>
<li>The condition can be self-limiting or can progress to fibrosis (scarring), cirrhosis or liver cancer.</li>
<li><strong>Hepatitis viruses</strong> are the most common cause of hepatitis in the world but other infections, toxic substances (e.g. alcohol, certain drugs), and autoimmune diseases can also cause hepatitis..</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The disease is found in all the countries of the world. There are five types of viruses which cause hepatitis. These are:
a) Hepatitis A Virus (HAV)
b) Hepatitis B Virus (HBV)
c) Hepatitis C Virus (HCV)
d) Hepatitis D Virus (HDV)
e) Hepatitis E Virus (HEV)</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hepatitis-a-virus-hav">Hepatitis A virus (HAV)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hepatitis-a-virus-hav" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Is present in the faeces of infected persons and is most often transmitted through consumption of contaminated water or food.</li>
<li>Certain sex practices can also spread HAV. Infections are in many cases mild, with most people making a full recovery and remaining immune from further HAV infections.</li>
<li>However, HAV infections can also be severe and life threatening. Most people in areas of the world with poor sanitation have been infected with this virus. Safe and effective vaccines are available to prevent HAV.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hepatitis-b-virus-hbv">Hepatitis B virus (HBV)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hepatitis-b-virus-hbv" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Is transmitted through exposure to infective blood, semen, and other body fluids.</li>
<li>HBV can be transmitted from infected mothers to infants at the time of birth or from family member to infant in early childhood.</li>
<li>Transmission may also occur through transfusions of HBV-contaminated blood and blood products, contaminated injections during medical procedures, and through injection drug use.</li>
<li>HBV also poses a risk to healthcare workers who sustain accidental needle stick injuries while caring for infected-HBV patients. Safe and effective vaccines are available to prevent HBV.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>^{}[]</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hepatitis-c-virus-hcv">Hepatitis C virus (HCV)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hepatitis-c-virus-hcv" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Is mostly transmitted through exposure to infective blood.</li>
<li>This may happen through transfusions of HCV-contaminated blood and blood products, contaminated injections during medical procedures, and through injection drug use.</li>
<li>Sexual transmission is also possible, but is much less common. There is no vaccine for HCV.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hepatitis-d-virus-hdv">Hepatitis D virus (HDV)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hepatitis-d-virus-hdv" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Infections occur only in those who are infected with HBV. The dual infection of HDV and HBV can result in a more serious disease and worse outcome. Hepatitis B vaccines provide protection from HDV infection.</li>
<li>Hepatitis E virus (HEV) is mostly transmitted through consumption of contaminated water or food. HEV is a common cause of hepatitis outbreaks in developing parts of the world and is increasingly recognized as an important cause of disease in developed countries</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mode-of-transmission">Mode of transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mode-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hepatitis A and E infections are transmitted through faecal-oral route and are both called infectious hepatitis.</li>
<li>Hepatitis B, C and D are transmitted through blood products and close personal contacts and are called serum hepatitis. Serum hepatitis may cause chronic liver infection and liver cirrhosis.</li>
<li>The human being is the only known reservoir and host of viral hepatitis.</li>
<li>The disease is transmitted from the infected person to the susceptible host through faeces, contaminated food and objects, blood, blood serum and other body fluids.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">Cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>In the case of hepatitis B infection, transmission takes place through two main routes:</li>
<li>Percutaneous route - this is through injections and transfusion of blood and blood products.</li>
<li>Non-percutaneous routes - these include close personal contact for example, kissing and sexual intercourse, from mother to foetus through placenta or to baby during delivery.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>All types of hepatitis infections are characterised by a similar clinical picture.</li>
<li>The incubation period is one to four weeks in the case of hepatitis A and 12 weeks or longer in the case of hepatitis B.</li>
<li>Hepatitis infections manifest in two phases.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pre-icteric-phase-no-jaundice">Pre-icteric Phase (no jaundice)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pre-icteric-phase-no-jaundice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Fever of sudden onset</li>
<li>Malaise</li>
<li>Loss of appetite</li>
<li>Nausea</li>
<li>Abdominal discomfort</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="icteric-phase">Icteric Phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#icteric-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Appearance of jaundice</li>
<li>Enlarged tender liver (hepatomegaly)</li>
<li>Extreme tiredness and myalgia</li>
<li>Feelings of deep sadness (depression)</li>
<li>Pale stools</li>
<li>Dark urine (contains bilirubin)</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="people-at-risk-of-hepatitis">People At Risk of Hepatitis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#people-at-risk-of-hepatitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Reservoirs of hepatitis B virus include:</li>
<li>Sexually promiscuous individuals,</li>
<li>Spouses of acutely infected persons</li>
<li>Health care workers exposed to blood</li>
<li>Family members of chronically infected persons</li>
<li>Anyone who requires repeated blood transfusions</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The urine of a person suffering from viral hepatitis is dark and contains bilirubin, while the stool is usually pale.</li>
<li>In the blood, both direct and indirect bilirubin levels are raised.</li>
<li>In the case of hepatitis B, diagnosis is made by detecting various immunological markers in the blood.</li>
<li>The most important is the hepatitis B surface antigen (HBsAg) which is present when the virus is in the blood in the acute stage and in the chronic carrier state.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>No specific treatment is available for both hepatitis A and B.</li>
<li>The patient should be given symptomatic treatment together with diet and bed rest at home to prevent the spread of the disease.</li>
<li>If admission is indicated for one reason or the other, you should ensure that the patient is isolated and extra precautions taken during handling and disposal of excreta.</li>
<li>Since alcohol increases the risk of cirrhosis, you should advise the patient to avoid alcohol for at least six months</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Improvement of environmental sanitation will prevent the transmission of hepatitis</li>
<li>Isolating patients suffering viral hepatitis</li>
<li>Administration of hepatitis vaccine</li>
<li>Screening blood for hepatitis B surface antigen before giving it for transfusion and excluding all donors with a history of jaundice</li>
<li>Effective sterilisation and high level disinfection of all instruments, needles and syringes</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="specific-preventive-measures-for-hepatitis-b">Specific preventive measures for hepatitis B<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#specific-preventive-measures-for-hepatitis-b" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Vaccination</li>
<li>Wash your hands thoroughly after any potential exposure</li>
<li>Practice safe sex with all partners</li>
<li>Avoid direct contact with blood and bodily fluids</li>
<li>Clean up blood spills with a fresh diluted bleach solution</li>
<li>Cover all cuts carefully</li>
<li>Avoid sharing sharp items such as razors, nail clippers, toothbrushes, and earrings or body rings</li>
<li>Discard sanitary napkins and tampons into plastic bags</li>
<li>Avoid illegal street drugs (injecting, inhaling, snorting, popping pills)</li>
<li>Do not donate blood or body organs</li>
<li>Make sure new, sterile needles are used for ear or body piercing, tattoos, and acupuncture</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
BUREAU VERITAS 1828</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="enteric-fevers">ENTERIC FEVERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#enteric-fevers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Enteric fevers include typhoid fever and paratyphoid A and B fevers.</li>
<li>Typhoid fever is an infectious disease characterised by high continuous fever, malaise and involvement of lymphoid tissue and spleen.</li>
<li>Diarrhoea is not a common symptom in typhoid fever.</li>
<li>Paratyphoid fever may present like typhoid fever, but in most cases it presents as gastroenteritis or transient diarrhoea.</li>
<li>Both are mainly spread by the faecal-oral route through contaminated food, water and milk. Flies are also important in the transmission of enteric fevers.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="typhoid-fever">TYPHOID FEVER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#typhoid-fever" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This is an infectious bacterial disease caused by <em>salmonella typhi</em>.</li>
<li>Epidemic outbreaks have occurred when a source of water or food used by many people has been contaminated</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The incubation period of typhoid fever is 7 - 21 days. The disease has a gradual onset which progresses through the following four stages.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="first-week">First Week<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#first-week" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>During the first week and early in the disease, the patient has severe headache, malaise, loss of appetite, body pains and aches and a tendency to nose-bleed.</li>
<li>The body temperature rises day by day or in steps to 39.5C or higher. Most patients cough because they develop bronchitis and may also complain of constipation.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="second-week">Second Week<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#second-week" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>In the second week, temperature continues to rise, but the pulse rate is slower than would be expected for that temperature. There is swelling of lymphoid tissue in the intestines as well as Peyer's patches, necrosis and ulcers, which cause the abdomen to become distended and tender.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The high temperature and toxaemia causes mental confusion and disorientation in the patient. Half the patients may develop greenish watery ('pea-soup') diarrhoea and broncho-pneumonia.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="third-week">Third Week<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#third-week" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Body temperature decreases step by step and the patient improves slowly. If there is no improvement, the Peyer's patches in the intestines perforate and toxaemia increases.</li>
<li>The patient becomes delirious and incontinent of urine and stool, muscles twitch and coma may precede death.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fourth-week">Fourth Week<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fourth-week" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>For the patients who do not suffer the serious complications of the third week, the fourth week is a period of convalescence.</li>
<li>The temperature drops back to normal and the patient recovers gradually</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The best way to diagnose typhoid fever is through a <strong>blood culture</strong>.</li>
<li>This may be positive during the first week and for a variable period after this.</li>
<li>Stool and urine cultures can also be made although they are only positive after the first week.</li>
<li>Other important diagnostic tests include:</li>
<li><strong>Widal Test</strong> is an agglutination test which detects the presence of serum antibodies (H and O) in patients serum with typhoid and paratyphoid fever</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A widal test of 1:80 or and 1:160 should be considered as clinically significant (active infection). That typhoid is present.</li>
<li>Although the Widal test is still very useful, especially when two tests are performed four to five days apart after the end of the first week, its interpretation is full of difficulties especially in endemic areas and in people who have had the typhoid vaccine</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Fluid replacement due to diarrhoea</li>
<li>Oral norfloxacin 400mg 12 hourly for 10 - 14 days</li>
<li>Oral ciproxacin 500mg bd. for 14 days</li>
<li>Contaminated articles should be disposed by incineration</li>
<li>Stools and urine should be disposed of in a pit latrine or septic tank</li>
<li>Surgical treatment for perforated bowels</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Identification of the carriers especially those who work as food handlers and treat them promptly</li>
<li>Administration of typhoid vaccine</li>
<li>Safe water supply</li>
<li>Improvement in food hygiene</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="summary">summary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>When you see the following signs and symptoms, then you need to suspect the presence of typhoid.</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Fever that starts low and increases daily, possibly reaching as high as 40.5 C</li>
<li>Headache</li>
<li>Weakness and fatigue</li>
<li>Muscle aches</li>
<li>Sweating</li>
<li>Dry cough</li>
<li>Loss of appetite and weight loss</li>
<li>Abdominal pain</li>
<li>Diarrhea or constipation</li>
<li>Rash</li>
<li>Extremely swollen abdomen</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="kenya-medical-training-college">KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kenya-medical-training-college" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
