<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tapeworm-taeniasis">Tapeworm (Taeniasis)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tapeworm-taeniasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Belong to group of Flat worms with hydatid.</li>
<li>There are various types of tapeworms, but in human beings the infestations are commonly caused by:</li>
<li>Taenia saginata or beef tapeworm (commonest infection)</li>
<li>Taenia solium or pork tapeworm</li>
<li>Taenia Saginata or Beef Tapeworm</li>
<li>Infection with the beef tapeworm is common in areas where beef is eaten raw or lightly cooked</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mode-of-transmission">Mode of Transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mode-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The eggs of adult tapeworms living in the small intestines of human beings are passed in the stools.</li>
<li>They are then ingested by cows as they feed on contaminated grass.</li>
<li>Once in the gastrointestinal tract of the cow, the embryos hatch and penetrate the bowel wall and are carried via the bloodstream to striated muscles.</li>
<li>Here the larvae grow and form infective cysts called cysticerci.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>When human beings ingest cow meat containing these cysts, the cysts are dissolved by the gastric acid in the stomach to release embryos</li>
<li><strong>Clinical Features</strong></li>
<li>Loss of weight</li>
<li>Abdominal discomfort</li>
<li>Itching around the anus (pruritis ani).</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Drug treatment with oral niclosamide is effective.</li>
<li>The dose is 1gm chewed and swallowed with water followed one hour later with 1gm (a total of 2gm).</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS 001</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="taenia-solium-pork-tapeworm">Taenia Solium (Pork Tapeworm)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#taenia-solium-pork-tapeworm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This disease occurs when a person ingests pork infected with the taenia solium larvae.</li>
<li>Whereas in the beef tapeworm the embryo attaches itself to the wall of the small bowel and grows into an adult worm, the pork tapeworm behaves differently.</li>
<li>The embryo penetrates the intestinal wall of the human as it does the pig, and it is carried to organs like striated muscle or the brain. This can cause serious problems such as epilepsy and death</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Taenia solium is a dangerous worm and the signs and symptoms depend on the organ it has invaded as follows:</li>
<li>In the brain it causes epilepsy</li>
<li>In the skeletal muscles it causes myositis (severe pain), which may make movement temporarily impossible</li>
<li>In the laryngeal muscles it causes difficulty in speaking</li>
<li>In the myocardium it causes (myocarditis), heart failure or cardiac arrest</li>
<li>In the eyeball it can cause unilateral or bilateral blindness</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Diagnosis
Diagnosis of taenia solium infections can be made by doing the following tests:</li>
<li>Biopsy examination of the infected tissue</li>
<li>X-ray examination to locate the calcified cysticercus</li>
<li>Stool microscopy for ova and cyst</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Surgical removal of calcified cysticercus where possible as well as drug treatment with niclosamide 2gm.</li>
<li>The dose is 1gm chewed and washed down with water followed one hour later by 1gm.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Proper disposal of human faeces in toilets instead of in the field and within reach of cattle and pigs</li>
<li>Ensuring that beef, pork and fish are thoroughly cooked</li>
<li>Eating only meats that have been inspected</li>
<li>Burying in deep pits or incinerating the carcasses of heavily infected cattle and pigs</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="strongyloidiasis">STRONGYLOIDIASIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#strongyloidiasis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Strongyloidiasis is a chronic parasitic infection of humans caused by <em>Strongyloides stercoralis</em> (and rarely <em>S. flleborni</em>)</li>
<li>Transmission occurs mainly in tropical and subtropical regions but also in countries with temperate climates.</li>
<li>Infection is acquired through direct contact with contaminated soil during agricultural, domestic and recreational activities.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="transmission-cycle">Transmission cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#transmission-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Strongyloidiasis is transmitted through direct penetration of human skin by infective larvae when in contact with soil.</li>
<li>Walking barefoot is therefore a major risk factor for acquiring the infection.</li>
<li>Strongyloides spp. Larvae penetrate the human host and reach the intestine where they mature into adults and produce eggs</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>The eggs hatch in the gut lumen and yield larvae that are evacuated in faeces.</li>
<li>The peculiarity of this worm is that some larvae are not excreted but reinvade the intestine or perianal skin to perpetuate the infection ("autoinfection cycle").</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="symptoms">Symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Is usually asymptomatic and if symptoms are present, they include:</p>
<p> Upper abdominal pain or burning.
 Diarrhea or alternating diarrhea and constipation.
 A cough.
 A rash.
 Red hives near the anus {urticaria}
 Vomiting.
 Weight loss.</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The gold standard for the diagnosis of Strongyloides is serial stool examination for Ova.</li>
<li>Duodenal aspirate is more sensitive than stool examination, and duodenal biopsy may reveal parasites in the gastric and duodenal glands</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treament">Treament<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treament" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>First line therapy
Ivermectin, in a single dose, 200 g/kg orally for 1-2 days</li>
<li>Alternative</li>
<li>Albendazole, 400 mg orally two times a day for 7 days.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The best way to prevent <strong>strongyloides</strong> infection is to wear shoes walking on soil</li>
<li>Avoid contact with fecal matter or sewage.</li>
<li>Proper sewage disposal and fecal management</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="poliomyelitis">POLIOMYELITIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#poliomyelitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Poliomyelitis is an acute infectious viral disease of the anterior horn cells of the spinal cord and sometimes of the lower part of the brain.</li>
<li>The anterior horn cell is a portion of the spinal cord that contains the motor neurons responsible for body's axial muscles. It forms the grey matter</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It usually affects children under five but more commonly children under three.</li>
<li>It is characterised by varying degrees of paralysis</li>
<li>Also known as infantile paralysis or polio</li>
<li>Infection with polio give a life long immunity</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Causal organism : poliovirus</li>
<li>They are of three types ;</li>
<li>Type one is known as Brunhilde, which is the most frequent cause of paralytic illness and responsible for epidemics.</li>
<li>Type two is called Lansing: Responsible for sporadic cases</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCES</p>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Type three is known as Leon. The latter two are less commonly associated with paralysis</li>
<li>Reseirvor of infection: Man is the only reseirvor. Virus is present in throat and intestine. Feacal and oropharyngeal secretions are infectious material</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mode-of-transmission">Mode of transmission<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mode-of-transmission" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>There two are main routes of transmission:</li>
<li> Feacal/oral route: Through contaminated water, food, fingers, milk etc, where hygiene is poor.</li>
<li> Droplet infection: Droplet spread from coughing and sneezing during acute stage.</li>
<li>Incubation period: 7 to 14 days</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Source of virus: feces and oropharyngeal secretions of infected persons.</li>
<li>The Fives F's are common routes of entry. They include: Fingers, Flies, Faeces, Fluids</li>
<li>and Food</li>
<li>Period of communicability: virus is present in throat and feces shortly after infection and persists for about 1 week in throat and 4-6 weeks in feces</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="risk-factors">Risk factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The virus enters into the mouth
Replication starts in pharynx, GI tract, local lymphatics
Hematologic spread to lymphatics and central nervous system
Viral spread along nerve fibers
Destruction of motor neurons leading to paralysis</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-presentation">Clinical presentation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Clinical signs and symptoms are grouped into four</li>
</ul>
<p> Prodromal or minor illness stage characterized by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Fever, headache, irritability, Coryza, sorethroat, cough, vomiting, diarrhoea or constipation</li>
</ul>
<p> Major illness stage is divided into three stages:
a) Preparalytic stage: fever of 39-40 C, headache, malaise, vomiting, anorexia and diarrhoea. Symptoms disappear after 1-2 days or progress to paralytic stage.</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a) Paralytic stage: paralysis appear at any side of the body and is assymmetrical. Lower limbs are more affected than upper limb. Spread of paralysis is usually completed in 24 hours. There is pain in paralysed muscles</p>
<p>b) Post paralytic stage: paralysis of muscles leads to deformity and contractures. There may be retardation of bone growth resulting in shortening of the affected limb</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="factors-that-increases-risk-of-paralysis">Factors that increases risk of paralysis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-that-increases-risk-of-paralysis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Immune deficiency</li>
<li>Malnutrition</li>
<li>Tonsillectomy</li>
<li>Physical activity immediately following the onset of paralysis</li>
<li>Skeletal muscle injury due to injection of vaccines or therapeutic agents</li>
<li>Pregnancy</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnostic-categories-for-people-who-acquire-viral-infection-from-polio-virus">Diagnostic categories for people who acquire viral infection from polio virus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-categories-for-people-who-acquire-viral-infection-from-polio-virus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Abortive Polio: Symptoms do not include neurologic symptoms. Mainly gastrointestinal upset: Malaise, anorexia, vomiting, fever, headache and sore throat. Polio virus can be isolated from throat washings and stool. Interpretation: Polio virus growing in gut and throat lymphatic tissue and has not migrated to the spinal cord or brain</li>
<li>Non-paralytic Polio: Symptoms include neurological symptoms: Headache, stiff neck, muscle stiffness and spasms along with other muscular symptoms</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Paralytic poliomyelitis, experienced in &lt;1% of poliovirus infections, occurs when the virus enters the central nervous system and replicates in anterior horn cells (motor neurons) of the spinal cord. When it multiplies in the nervous system, the virus can destroy nerve cells (motor neurons) which activate skeletal muscles. The affected muscles lose their function due to a lack of nervous innervation, a condition known as acute flaccid paralysis.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="continue">continue<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#continue" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Paralytic polio is divided into two forms:</li>
<li> Spinal polio : Most common form of paralytic poliomyelitis  Viral invasion of the motor neurons of the anterior horn cells leads to paralysis of limbs</li>
<li> Bulbar polio : Bulbar region is the white matter in the brain that connects cerebral cortex to brain stem. Destruction of this region weakens the muscles supplied by the cranial nerves, producing symptoms of encephalitis, and causes difficult breathing, speaking and swallowing</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Nerves affected:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Glossopharyngeal nerve - difficult swallowing, impaired throat, tongue movement and taste</li>
<li>Vagus nerve - the heart, intestines, and lungs.</li>
<li>Accessory nerve - upper neck movement.</li>
<li>Trigeminal nerve and facial nerve - the cheeks, tear ducts, gums, and muscles of the face, double vision; difficulty in chewing; abnormal respiratory rate, depth, and rhythmrespiratory arrest. Pulmonary edema and shock also possible, and may be fatal</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>No specific drug is available</li>
<li>Absolute bed rest in preparalytic stage until it is certain that paralysis will not develop</li>
<li>Avoid all injection to prevent precipitating paralysis</li>
<li>Maintain passive movement of the affected limb to prevent contractures</li>
<li>Active physiotherapy in post paralytic stage to reduce disability</li>
<li>Assisted respiratory ventilation in case of respiratory paralysis</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS 001</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The patient is to be nursed in isolation</li>
<li>Pain is controlled through the administration of analgesics, for example, paracetamol, valium or phenorbabitone.</li>
<li>Regular respiratory suction and postural drainage should be performed</li>
<li>N.G tube feeding with high calorie and include substantial amounts of protein</li>
<li>Change the patient's position every four hours to prevent bedsores</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Active immunization using OPV and IPV as the last dose</li>
<li>Report about the case to health authorities at once</li>
<li>Isolate the patient for one week from the date of onset of the disease or as long as the fever last.</li>
<li>Proper disposal of urine and feaces of the patient</li>
<li>Immunize all contacts and ensure high coverage in the community</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li> Protection of all sources of water during outbreaks</li>
<li> Milk must be pasteurized and fruit should be washed with weak permanganate solution before using</li>
<li> Avoid overcrowding of children in schools, play grounds etc</li>
<li> Educate people about disease and its consequences</li>
<li> Search of sick persons and investigation of contacts to establish the source of infections</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-polio-outbreaks">Management of polio outbreaks<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-polio-outbreaks" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<li>Confirm cases by sending fresh stool samples to the nearest reference laboratory</li>
<li>Active immunisation of all under fives in the region</li>
<li>Post pone other injectable immunisations</li>
<li>Restrict use of all injections in health facilities</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tetanus">TETANUS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tetanus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>An infectious disease caused by contamination of wounds from the bacteria <em>Clostridium tetani</em>, or the spores they produce that live in the soil, and animal feces</li>
<li>It is characterised by increased muscle tone and spasms that present as painful contractions of voluntary muscles.</li>
<li><em>Clostridium tetani</em> is a rod shape, Anaerobic gram-positive, spore-forming bacteria</li>
<li>It is an obligate anaerobe meaning that the organism live and multiply in absence of oxygen</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>T</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Tetanus is also called lockjaw.</li>
<li>It is caused by toxin produced by C.Tetani called <strong>Neurotoxin or tetanospasmin</strong>: It is a protein in nature and responsible for the characteristic signs of tetanus</li>
<li>It also produces another toxin called <strong>Hemolysin or tetanolysin</strong>: It is a potent lethal toxin</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Reservoir : Soil and intestine of animals and humans</li>
<li>Transmission: Contaminated wounds and Tissue injury</li>
<li>Temporal pattern : Peak in summer or wet season</li>
<li>Communicability : Not contagious</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="habitat-of-tetanus-bacilli">Habitat of tetanus bacilli<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#habitat-of-tetanus-bacilli" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Tetanus bacilli live in bowels of animals and sometimes human.</li>
<li>When bacilli are passed out in feaces, they form spores in order to survive the harsh conditions outside</li>
<li>The spores are found throughout the environment, usually in soil, dust, and animal waste</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Tetanus bacilli continue their life cycle when the spores are swallowed by animal and humans</li>
<li>Tetanus is acquired through contact with the environment; it is not transmitted from person to person.</li>
<li>Anaerobic conditions allow germination of spores and production of toxins</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="routes-of-entry">Routes of entry<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#routes-of-entry" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The usual locations for the bacteria to enter the body:</li>
<li>Puncture wounds (such as those caused by rusty nails, splinters, or insect bites.)</li>
<li>Burns, or any break in the skin, and IV drug access sites are also potential entryways for the bacteria.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Animal bites/human bites</li>
<li>Open fractures</li>
<li>Gangrene</li>
<li>In neonates usually via infected umbilical stumps</li>
<li>Abscess</li>
<li>Parenteral drug abuse</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="wounds-which-favor-growth-of-clostridium-tetani">Wounds which favor growth of Clostridium tetani<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#wounds-which-favor-growth-of-clostridium-tetani" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Necrotic Umbilical stump in newborn</li>
<li>Crush wounds {necrosis, poor blood supply}</li>
<li>Stab deep wounds</li>
<li>Wounds with foreign bodies</li>
<li>Burns</li>
<li>Endometritis {after abortion or child birth from the use of poorly sterilised instruments}</li>
<li>Surgical wounds</li>
<li>Chronic ulcers</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>C. tetani enters body from through wound</li>
<li>Stays in sporulated form until anaerobic conditions are presented</li>
<li>Germinates under anaerobic conditions and begins to multiply and produce tetrospasmin</li>
<li>Tetanospasmin spreads using blood and lymphatic system, and binds to motor neurons</li>
<li>Travels along the axons to the spinal cord</li>
<li>Binds to sites responsible for inhibiting skeletal muscle contraction</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features">Clinical features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Incubation period is 5-21 days but it can range from 3 days to 3 months</li>
</ul>
<p>Common signs and symptoms of tetanus include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Spasms and stiffness in jaw muscles (trismus)</li>
<li>Stiffness of neck muscles</li>
<li>Difficulty swallowing</li>
<li>Stiffness of abdominal muscles</li>
<li>Painful body spasms lasting for several minutes,</li>
<li>There may be high fever and hypertension.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>1</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Death usually occur due to asphyxia and exhaustion.</li>
<li>Asphyxia may be due to:</li>
<li> Spasm of glottis, thoracic muscles, diaphragm</li>
<li> Chronic hypoventilation because of muscle stiffness</li>
<li> Periods of apnoea</li>
<li> Aspiration of feeds and respiratory secretions and subsequent suffocation</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="symptoms-in-newborn">Symptoms in newborn<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms-in-newborn" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Tetanus in newborn is called Tetanus neonatorum.</li>
<li>The first sign in newborn is inability to suck for a baby who was doing well after delivery</li>
<li>Spasms develop later accompanied by severe apnoea and cyanosis</li>
<li>A typical feature is the extended spine with clenched fists, irritability, locked jaw and flexed toes</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCES</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="period-of-onset">Period of onset<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#period-of-onset" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It is the time from first symptoms to the reflex spasm.</li>
<li>A period of onset of less than 48 hr is associated with the development of severe tetanus.</li>
<li>The shorter the incubation period and the onset time, the more fulminating the disease</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tetanus-toxin-transport">Tetanus toxin transport<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tetanus-toxin-transport" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Initially binds to peripheral nerve terminals</li>
<li>Transported within the axon and across synaptic junctions until it reaches the central nervous system.</li>
</ul>
<p>How does the toxin acts?</p>
<ul>
<li>Blocks the release of inhibitory neurotransmitters (glycine and gamma-amino butyric acid) across the synaptic cleft, which is required to check the nervous impulse.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>If nervous impulses cannot be checked by normal inhibitory mechanisms, it leads to unopposed muscular contraction and spasms that are characteristic of tetanus</li>
<li>Diagnosis</li>
<li>There are currently no blood tests that can be used to diagnose tetanus. Diagnosis is done clinically.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principles-of-treatment">Principles of Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Neutralization of unbound toxin with Human tetanus immunoglobulin. It is antitoxin given 10,000IU IM or IV.A test dose is given while keeping adrenaline at hand because allergic reactions are common and severe</li>
<li>Prevention of further toxin production by eliminating the source of toxin through:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Wound debridement</li>
<li>Antibiotics (Metronidazole) and penicillins eradicate vegetative cells the source of toxins</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS 0004</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<ol start="3">
<li>Control of muscle spasms through:</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>IV diazepam 10-40mg start</li>
<li>maintain sedation by giving crushed tablets every 3 hours through the Nasogastric tube.</li>
<li>avoid unnecessary stimuli. Nurse the patient in a quiet dark room to minimise provoked spams</li>
<li>Protecting the airway</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="4-supportive-care">4. Supportive care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-supportive-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Bedrest with a nonstimulating environment (dim light, reduced noise, and stable temperature) may be recommended.</p>
<ul>
<li>Sedation may be necessary to keep the affected person calm.</li>
<li>Respiratory support with oxygen, endotracheal tube, and mechanical ventilation may be necessary</li>
<li>Adequate hydration due to fluid losses resulting from autonomic dysfunction</li>
<li>Nutrition</li>
<li>Treatment of secondary infection</li>
<li>prevention of bed sores by turning the patient every two hours</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>Vaccination after recovery</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</strong></p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="actions-taken-at-the-dispensary">Actions taken at the dispensary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#actions-taken-at-the-dispensary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>If you are in dispensary and you suspect a patient has tetanus, take the following actions:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Control muscle spasms with either diazepam IM 10-40mg or Phernobarbitone 100mg plus chlorpromazine 50mg</li>
<li>Pass nasogastric tube</li>
<li>Repeat same dose of diazepam immediately by mouth</li>
<li>Give metronidazole 400mg TDS for 5 days</li>
<li>Write a letter of referral and transfer the patient</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tetanus-complications">Tetanus Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tetanus-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Laryngospasm</li>
<li>Fractures</li>
<li>Hypertension</li>
<li>Nosocomial infections</li>
<li>Pulmonary embolism</li>
<li>Aspiration</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Vaccinating a higher percentage of pregnant women against tetanus with vaccines containing tetanus toxoid (TT).</li>
<li>Vaccinating all females of childbearing age (approximately 1545 years) with TT vaccine in high-risk areas where vaccination coverage is currently low.</li>
<li>Promoting clean delivery and childcare practices, through better hygiene and care of the newborn's umbilicus.</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Proper surgical treatment of wounds such as removal of foreign bodies and excision of necrotic tissue</li>
<li>Improving surveillance and reporting of cases of neonatal tetanus. The case finding and reporting will help us to give appropriate treatment and vaccination to children</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="whooping-cough-pertussis">WHOOPING COUGH (PERTUSSIS)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#whooping-cough-pertussis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Is and infection of respiratory system caused by bacterium Bordetella pertussis.</li>
<li>Transmission: direct contact with droplets of an infected person, indirect contact with freshly contaminated articles</li>
<li>Incubation period: 6-20 days but usually 7-10 days</li>
<li>Period of communicability: greatest during catarrhal stage before onset of paroxysm</li>
<li>Paroxysms are sudden recurrence or intensification of symptoms</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Catarrhal stage; runny nose, sneezing, low grade fever.</p>
<ul>
<li>Paroxysmal stage: cough most often occurs at night and consist of short rapid coughs with high pitch crowing sound called whoop. During paroxysms cheeks become flushed or cyanotic, eyes bulge and tongue protrudes. Vomiting frequently follows attack. The stage lasts 4-6 weeks</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stages-of-whooping-cough">Stages of whooping cough<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stages-of-whooping-cough" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Stage 1 (Catarrhal stage):</li>
<li>Cold, runny nose and irritating cough</li>
<li>Most infectious stage. Last for 14 days</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stage-2-paroxysmal-stage">Stage 2 (Paroxysmal stage):<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stage-2-paroxysmal-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Severe series of coughs usually ending with a high-pitched whoop</li>
<li>The whoop starts 1 to 2 weeks after the cold symptoms and lasts 6 weeks to 3 months</li>
<li>Thick, clear, sticky mucous may be coughed up at the end of the coughing spasm</li>
<li>Coughing spasms are more frequent at night</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>BUREAU VERITAS 1828</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stage-3-convalescent-stage">Stage 3 (Convalescent stage):<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stage-3-convalescent-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Gradual disappearance of symptoms occurring over 2 to 4 weeks, however, coughing spells can last for weeks or months</li>
<li>Cough may become louder and may sound like it is getting worse as the person is getting better</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology-of-pertusis">Pathophysiology of pertusis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology-of-pertusis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Bacteria attaches to cilia of ciliated epithelial cells in respiratory tract</li>
<li>Pertussis antigens allow evasion of host defenses</li>
<li>Causes local tissue damage in respiratory tract leading to manifestations of symptoms</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS 001</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The newer macrolides (azithromycin and clarithromycin) have good acitivity against <em>B pertussis</em>.</li>
<li>Clarithromycin (500 mg bid) used for 10  14 days and Azithromycin (500 mg/d) used for 5  7 days have been used with good results</li>
<li>Steroids may reduce the number and severity of cough paroxysms, but are generally only recommended for infants with serious disease</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">Cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Encourage fluids; offer small amounts of fluids frequently</li>
<li>Observe for signs of airway obstruction such as cyanosis, retractions, increased restlessness</li>
<li>Administer oxygen if dyspnea and cyanosis is present</li>
<li>Give adequate fluids.</li>
<li>Intubation possibly necessary incase of airway obstruction</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Provide restful environment and reduce factors that promote paroxysm such as dust, smoke, sudden change in temperature, chilling, activity, excitement. Keep room well ventilated.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">COMPLICATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Pneumonia</li>
<li>Atelectasis</li>
<li>Otitis media</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Convulsions</li>
<li>Hemorrhage; subarachnoid, subconjunctival and epistaxis</li>
<li>Dehydration</li>
<li>Weight loss</li>

<li>Hand washing after handling secretions.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mumps-infective-or-epidemic-parotitis">Mumps(Infective or Epidemic Parotitis)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mumps-infective-or-epidemic-parotitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This is a viral infectious disease of the parotid glands that can also affect other glands.</li>
<li>It is characterized by painful swellings of salivary glands</li>
<li>Causal organism : paramyxovirus</li>
<li>Transmission : droplets or contact with the salivary secretions of the infected person.</li>
<li>Incubation period : 14-21 days
period of communicability : most communicable immediately before and after swelling begins</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Prodromal stage: fever, headache, malaise and anorexia for 24hrs followed by earache that is aggravated by chewing.</li>
<li>Enlargement of parotid gland accompanied by pain and tenderness (parotitis)</li>
<li><strong>Complications</strong></li>
<li>Orchitis: inflammation of one or both of the testicles.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>Oophoritis: inflammation of an ovary. Presents with severe lower abdominal pain and vomiting</li>
<li>Prostatitis: inflammation of the prostate gland. It is characterized by unexplained fever and dysuria</li>
<li>Mastitis: inflammation of the mammary gland in the breast. Characterized by pain and swelling</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Pancreatitis : inflammation of the pancreas. Presents with severe upper abdominal pain, vomiting and fever</li>
<li>Meningitis ; inflammation of meninges ., presents with headache, fever, vomiting and neck rigidity</li>
<li>Encephalitis : inflammation of the brain tissue. presents with severe headache, fever, vomiting, convulsions, cranial nerve palsies</li>
</ul>
