<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="maternal-mortality-rate-mmr">Maternal mortality rate (MMR)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maternal-mortality-rate-mmr" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This is a measure of the number of women who die as a result of child bearing in a given year per 100,000 live births i.e.</li>
</ul>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mtext>MMR</mtext><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mrow><mtext>number&nbsp;of&nbsp;maternal&nbsp;deaths&nbsp;due&nbsp;to&nbsp;child&nbsp;bearing</mtext><mo></mo><mn>100</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>000</mn></mrow><mtext>number&nbsp;of&nbsp;live&nbsp;births&nbsp;that&nbsp;year</mtext></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\text{MMR} = \frac{\text{number of maternal deaths due to child bearing} \times 100,000}{\text{number of live births that year}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">MMR</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 2.2519em; vertical-align: -0.8804em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.3714em;"><span style="top: -2.314em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">number&nbsp;of&nbsp;live&nbsp;births&nbsp;that&nbsp;year</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.677em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">number&nbsp;of&nbsp;maternal&nbsp;deaths&nbsp;due&nbsp;to&nbsp;child&nbsp;bearing</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mord">100</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord">000</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s"></span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8804em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span></div>
<ul>
<li>Note: As is the case for infant mortality rate, the value of K is universally specified at 100,000 live births for international uniformity.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS 001</p>
<p>cont</p>
<ul>
<li>According to the World Health Organization (WHO), maternal death is defined as the death of a woman while pregnant or within 42 days of termination of pregnancy, irrespective of the duration and site of the pregnancy, from any cause related to or aggravated by the pregnancy or its management but not from accidental or incidental causes</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="case-fatality-rate-cfr">Case fatality rate (CFR)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#case-fatality-rate-cfr" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This measures the proportion of episodes of illness that result in death.</li>
<li>It is therefore the number of people who die from a disease out of all those who had the disease within a given period of time i.e.</li>
</ul>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mtext>CFR</mtext><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mtext>number&nbsp;of&nbsp;deaths&nbsp;due&nbsp;to&nbsp;a&nbsp;given&nbsp;disease</mtext><mtext>&nbsp;x&nbsp;100</mtext></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\text{CFR} = \frac{\text{number of deaths due to a given disease}}{\text{ x 100}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">CFR</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 2.0574em; vertical-align: -0.686em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.3714em;"><span style="top: -2.314em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">&nbsp;x&nbsp;100</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.677em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">number&nbsp;of&nbsp;deaths&nbsp;due&nbsp;to&nbsp;a&nbsp;given&nbsp;disease</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s"></span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.686em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span></div>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mtext>number&nbsp;of&nbsp;cases&nbsp;of&nbsp;that&nbsp;disease&nbsp;in&nbsp;a&nbsp;given&nbsp;period</mtext></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\text{number of cases of that disease in a given period}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">number&nbsp;of&nbsp;cases&nbsp;of&nbsp;that&nbsp;disease&nbsp;in&nbsp;a&nbsp;given&nbsp;period</span></span></span></span></span></span></div>
<ul>
<li>What percentage of people diagnosed with a certain disease die within a certain time after diagnosis</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Example
Assume a population of 100,000 people of who 40 are sick with cholera, and in one year (2012) period, 20 die from the disease.
What is the mortality rate?
= 20/100,000 died of cholera that year (2012)
= 0.02%
What is the case-fatality rate?
= 20/40 x100
= 50% or 50 per 100 people with cholera</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="early-neonatal-mortality-rate">Early neonatal mortality rate<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#early-neonatal-mortality-rate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Refers to a death of a live-born baby within the first seven days of life, while late neonatal mortality</li>
<li>covers the time after 7 days until before 28 days.</li>
<li>The sum of these two represents the neonatal mortality.</li>
<li>A neonatal death is defined as a death during the first 28 days of life (0-27 days).</li>
</ul>
<p>no. of neonatal deaths</p>
<p>neonatal mortality = ______ x 1000</p>
<p>rate Total no. of live births</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>BUREAU VERITAS 1828</p>
<p>The NMR is often broken down into early and late mortality rates.</p>
<p>The Early Neonatal Mortality rate (ENMR) is calculated as follows:</p>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mfrac><mtext>no.&nbsp;of&nbsp;neonatal&nbsp;deaths&nbsp;0-6&nbsp;days</mtext><mtext>x&nbsp;1000</mtext></mfrac><mo></mo><mn>1000</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\frac{\text{no. of neonatal deaths 0-6 days}}{\text{x 1000}} \times 1000</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 2.0574em; vertical-align: -0.686em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.3714em;"><span style="top: -2.314em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">x&nbsp;1000</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.677em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">no.&nbsp;of&nbsp;neonatal&nbsp;deaths&nbsp;0-6&nbsp;days</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s"></span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.686em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">1000</span></span></span></span></span></div>
<p><strong>Total no. of live births</strong></p>
<p>The late neonatal mortality rate (LNMR) is calculated as follows:</p>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mfrac><mtext>no.&nbsp;of&nbsp;neonatal&nbsp;deaths&nbsp;7-27&nbsp;days</mtext><mtext>x&nbsp;1000</mtext></mfrac><mo></mo><mn>1000</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\frac{\text{no. of neonatal deaths 7-27 days}}{\text{x 1000}} \times 1000</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 2.0574em; vertical-align: -0.686em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.3714em;"><span style="top: -2.314em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">x&nbsp;1000</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.677em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">no.&nbsp;of&nbsp;neonatal&nbsp;deaths&nbsp;7-27&nbsp;days</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s"></span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.686em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">1000</span></span></span></span></span></div>
<p><strong>Total no. of live births</strong></p>
<p>Neonatal mortality and post neonatal mortality (covering the remaining 11 months of the first year of life) are reflected in the Infant Mortality Rate.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ethical-considerations-in-community-diagnosis">Ethical Considerations in Community Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ethical-considerations-in-community-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>When conducting community diagnosis, it is very important to avoid taking any action that may be considered offensive by the community.</li>
<li>You need to make sure that the tools you use to collect information are not in any way offensive to the community.</li>
<li>They should not cause any physical, emotional, spiritual or cultural harm to that community</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>You should consider some of the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Obtaining permission to enter into the community boundaries</li>
<li>Obtaining informed consent before interviewing patients, families or groups</li>
<li>Establishing rapport before exploring sensitive areas</li>
<li>Ensuring confidentiality of the data collected</li>
<li>Selecting good interviewers</li>
<li>Training interviewers</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-process-of-community-diagnosis">THE PROCESS OF COMMUNITY DIAGNOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-process-of-community-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The process of community diagnosis requires careful planning right from the beginning.</li>
<li>It involves initial exploration and interaction with the community, planning of the survey, developing and pre-testing the survey tools and methods, and executing the survey and analysing the results</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The process of community diagnosis is made up of the following steps:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Exploration</li>
<li>Planning of the survey</li>
<li>Developing and pre-testing survey tools</li>
<li>Execution of the survey and data analysis</li>
<li>Report writing, dissemination and community action</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-exploring-the-community-community-inventory">1. Exploring the Community (Community Inventory)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-exploring-the-community-community-inventory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Exploration simply means mapping out of a community in order to learn or discover about it.</li>
<li>It is also known as community inventory.</li>
<li>Ideally, you should only carry out a community diagnosis after a request by the community or the people involved in providing health care.</li>
<li>The exploration phase is made up of three main activities:</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>I. Seeking permission and informing the various leaders
II. Seeking reactions of members of the community
III. Gathering background data about the community</p>
<ul>
<li>Although these activities are listed separately, they actually can take place at the same time</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="seeking-permission-and-informing-authorities-in-the-community">Seeking Permission and Informing Authorities in the Community<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#seeking-permission-and-informing-authorities-in-the-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>For the survey to succeed you must seek permission from community leaders.</li>
<li>Start by channelling your request through the official hierarchy of administrative leaders in that community:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Health personnel such as Medical Officer in Charge</li>
<li>Governmental officials such as Chiefs or District Officers</li>
<li>Community leaders through, for example, the village health committee</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>

Planning of the survey<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-planning-of-the-survey" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>During the planning phase, you should attempt to answer the following questions.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-why-is-the-survey-being-done">A. Why is the Survey Being Done?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-why-is-the-survey-being-done" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A survey is not carried out just to obtain interesting information.</li>
<li>There must be good reasons and the reasons must be useful to the community.</li>
<li>This question must therefore be answered to the satisfaction of all the leaders who are concerned with the community</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li>If the community has given you permission to carry out the survey, it will expect and have a right to expect some beneficial results from its cooperation.</li>
<li>You should therefore plan the survey with the intention of carrying out a proper action programme for the community. This information would most likely have been communicated during the exploratory phase</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li>Once the community leaders understand the reasons and are ready to cooperate with you, a meeting of the members of the community should be called to explain why there is a survey, why they have been chosen, what will be involved, when it will be done and what will happen to the results.</li>
<li>During this meeting you should invite government, health and community leaders so that the community can see who is supporting your work and who will be moving around their community and homes</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Where Will it Take Place?</li>
<li>You will have made this decision right at the beginning when exploring the community and seeking permission from various community and government leaders</li>
<li>Who Will be Interviewed?</li>
<li>It is usually not possible to interview everybody in a community unless of course it is very small</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>You will therefore need to select a sample from the total population which will be considered representative of what is happening in the entire population.</li>
<li>The sample could be made up of individuals or households depending on the available resources and time. There are certain techniques used to choose a sample.</li>
<li>It is also useful to talk to the local opinion leaders such as, the chief, village elders, members of organised groups such as church leaders and traditional healers, professionals in the area such as teachers and medical staff, and other extension workers.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>When Will the Survey Take Place?</li>
<li>If you intend to visit people at home, then you should avoid days when people are less likely to be at home, such as market days.</li>
<li>It is important to choose carefully the days when the interviewers will be in the field in order to ensure that they find the people they want to interview.</li>
<li>The exercise should also not coincide with seasons of important community activities such as planting, circumcision etc. Ideally you should decide when to conduct the survey after consulting the community members so that they are prepared for you.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="kenya-medical-training-college">KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kenya-medical-training-college" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>What Will be Covered in the Survey?</li>
<li>This will depend on what you want to learn about the community's health status and the information you have gathered during the exploratory phase.</li>
<li>Think of some of the common health problems that you see in your area for; children under five years, women aged from fifteen to forty nine years, and older people of sixty years and over.</li>
<li>You will agree that each group of people has its own unique problems..</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="kenya-medical-training-college">KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kenya-medical-training-college" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<p>Training for Better Health</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>What instruments will be used to measure the community's health status?
Usually questionnaires are used to cover most of the topics.</p>
<ul>
<li>However, in some instances, anthropometric measurements, physical examination and laboratory tests may also be necessary.</li>
</ul>
<p>How will data be collected and with what resources?</p>
<p>To answer this question you will need to specify the tasks that need to be done and then identify who will do them and how long it will take them</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Consider the following factors:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Time to travel to the study area</li>
<li>Time to locate the groups</li>
<li>Time and number of times each group will be visited. Allow time for following up defaulters</li>
<li>Calculate the number of interviews that can be completed in a day</li>
<li>Calculate the number of days that will be needed to complete the whole sample</li>
<li>Calculate the time needed for other parts of the study for example five days for preparation and pre-testing and twenty days for actual work</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>How do we select and train the official interviewers?
Ideally, the interviewers should come from the community so that they are well known to its members.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>School teachers, school children, health centre staff, village elders and young educated people are some of the people who can help you to survey your area and fill in the questionnaires.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>However, if your interviewers are not from that community, then you will need to introduce them to the community leaders and if possible to the community members in a public meeting.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Once the survey begins, they should wear identification badges and introduce themselves.</p>
</li>
</ul>

<li>Be able to establish good rapport with individuals, families or groups they will meet</li>
<li>Be good listeners and sensitive towards other people's feelings</li>
<li>Be able to relate well to the community members</li>

<li>Whenever possible, select people who speak the language of the study group.</li>
<li>The people who are selected as interviewers have different educational backgrounds from yours and may interpret questions and answers differently.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<li>The interviewers should understand the need to follow the questionnaire closely and in a standardised manner.</li>
<li>If each interviewer asks questions in their own manner the answers will be unreliable because they may refer to different things.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>During the training you should hold mock interviews with the interviewers so that you can ensure that each one of them can handle the assignment.</li>
<li>Use this opportunity to correct them and also to clarify issues about the questionnaire such as wrong translations and questions.</li>
<li>Once you are confident that your interviewers can handle the job, you should carry out a trial test or pilot test on a section of the community who have similar characteristics as the study group. This gives them a feel of the real situation and helps you to assess them further.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Interviewers should conduct themselves in an appropriate manner when approaching respondents. The points below should be followed:</p>
<ol>
<li>Establish rapport by greeting the respondents and introducing themselves</li>
<li>Explain carefully why they have come and what is the purpose of the survey</li>
<li>Ask if they are welcome to interview the family and if it is convenient for them at that time</li>
<li>Explain that they will be recording the information they collect</li>
<li>Emphasise that all information collected is confidential</li>
<li>Give them a chance to ask questions for clarification</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Having planned your survey and trained your interviewers, you now need to identify a representative sample which will answer your questions and provide you with the information and results you need.</li>
<li>You will now look at sampling.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sampling-for-a-survey">Sampling for a Survey<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sampling-for-a-survey" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Sampling is the process of selecting a number of individuals or units which will represent the larger group.</li>
<li>The aim is to get the same information from that sample that you would have got if the whole population had been surveyed.</li>
<li>For this reason, when you are selecting a sample for a survey, you must make sure that it is representative of the whole population.</li>
<li>You have to give an equal chance for each person in the population to be included in the sample. Otherwise you can come to wrong conclusions.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-study-population">A Study Population<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-study-population" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A study population is the entire group of individuals, events or objects that have common observable characteristics. For example:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> All first years in nursing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> All under fives in a given community</p>
</li>
<li>
<p> All qualified nurses with mental health qualifications</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This must be clearly defined for example, according to age, sex, or residence. A study population may also be selected for example, according to villages, institutions, records</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Each population is made up of study units identified by the type of problem that you want to study.</li>
<li>A study population can be divided into two main groups, namely, accessible population and the representative sample.</li>
<li>The accessible population is a group of individuals, objects and events with characteristics comparable to the target population and relevant to the study.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The representative sample is a group from the study population, which has all the important/relevant characteristics of the total population.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sampling-methods">Sampling Methods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sampling-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Before you sample you need to develop a sampling frame.</li>
<li>A sampling frame is a list of all units that make up the study population.</li>
<li>It enables you to sample the study units in such a way that the probability or the different units to be selected in the sample are known.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Sampling techniques fall under two main groups, namely, probability sampling and non probability sampling.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="probability-sampling">Probability Sampling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#probability-sampling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Probability sampling looks at the entire group of individuals, events or objects that have common observable characteristics</li>
<li>It has been found to give accurate results when one is studying groups that are too large to study in their entity.</li>
<li>It also provides an efficient system of capturing; in a small group the variations or similarities that exist in the target population</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="methods-of-probability-sampling">Methods of probability sampling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-probability-sampling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The following are the most commonly used methods in probability sampling:</p>
<ol>
<li>Simple random sampling</li>
<li>Systematic sampling</li>
<li>Stratified sampling</li>
<li>Cluster sampling</li>
<li>Multi-stage sampling</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-simple-random-sampling">1. Simple random sampling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-simple-random-sampling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A randomly selected sample from a larger sample or population, giving all the individuals in the sample an equal chance.</li>
<li>It means that every sampling unit in the population has an equal chance of being included in the sample</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-systematic-sampling">2. Systematic sampling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-systematic-sampling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>is a type of probability sampling method in which sample members from a larger population are selected according to a random starting point and a fixed, periodic interval.</p>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-stratified-sampling">3. Stratified Sampling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-stratified-sampling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>With stratified sampling, the researcher divides the population into separate groups, called strata with certain <strong>characteristics</strong>.</li>
<li>Then, a probability sample (often a simple random sample) is drawn from each group.</li>
<li>This method is used when the study population is very variable, for example, different ethnic groups, different ecological areas, or age groups. It allows you to subdivide the population into sub populations which are more homogeneous.</li>
<li>You then apply simple random sampling to each subgroup or stratum.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="4-cluster-sampling">4. Cluster Sampling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-cluster-sampling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Cluster sampling is accomplished by dividing the population into groups  usually <em>geographically</em>.</li>
<li>These groups are called clusters or blocks. The clusters are randomly selected, and each element in the selected clusters are used.</li>
<li>This method is used the population is either too large or scattered over a large geographical area.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS 001</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="5-multistage-sampling">5. Multistage sampling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-multistage-sampling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Multi-stage sampling represents a more complicated form of cluster sampling in which larger clusters are further subdivided into smaller, more targeted groupings for the purposes of surveying.</li>
<li>Despite its name, multi-stage sampling can in fact be easier to implement and can create a more representative sample of the population than a single sampling technique.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS 001</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="biased-sampling-or-non-probability-sampling-methods">Biased sampling or non-probability sampling methods.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#biased-sampling-or-non-probability-sampling-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Non probability sampling methods are used when a researcher is not interested in selecting a sample that is representative of the population.</li>
<li>They are mainly used in qualitative studies where the focus is on in-depth information rather than making generalisations.</li>
<li>Some examples of non-probability sampling methods are convenient sampling, quota sampling and purposive sampling.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-convenience-sampling">1. Convenience sampling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-convenience-sampling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Convenience sampling (also known as availability sampling) is a specific type of <strong>non-probability sampling</strong> method that relies on data collection from population members who are conveniently available to participate in study.</li>
<li>you select cases or units of observation as they become available.</li>
<li>For example, a health worker wanting to study attitudes of villagers towards family planning may decide to interview all adults visiting Maternal Child Health or Family Planning (MCH/FP) clinic on that day</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-quota-sampling">2. Quota Sampling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-quota-sampling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The researcher selects people according to some fixed quota. units are selected into a sample on the basis of pre-specified characteristics so that the total sample has the same distribution of characteristics assumed to exist in the population being studied, say for example, a certain religion or social class.</li>
<li>Quota sampling ensures that various groups or quotas of the population are included in the study according to some criteria.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-purposive-sampling">3. Purposive Sampling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-purposive-sampling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>purposive sampling is a sampling procedure where a researcher chooses specific people within the population to use for a particular study or research project.</li>
<li>the researcher simply picks individuals or cases that have the information or characteristics which they requires</li>
<li>The idea behind purposive sampling is to concentrate on people with particular characteristics who will better be able to assist with the relevant research.</li>
<li>Also known as judgmental, selective or subjective sampling</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="developing-and-pre-testing-tools-for-data-collection">DEVELOPING AND PRE-TESTING TOOLS FOR DATA COLLECTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#developing-and-pre-testing-tools-for-data-collection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Tools are implements that help us with our work</li>
<li>Before you embark on a community diagnosis survey you need to ensure that you have all the tools and instruments you need for measuring the community's health status. The tools used to measure a community's health status are:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Questionnaires</li>
<li>Focus group discussions</li>
<li>Measurements, physical examination and laboratory tests</li>
<li>Key informant interviews</li>
<li>Maps</li>
<li>Weighing scale</li>
<li>Specimen bottles</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="questionnaire">Questionnaire<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#questionnaire" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A questionnaire is a set of standardised questions designed to collect information about a specific aspect or issue in the community.</li>
<li>Before you design a questionnaire it is important for you to know what information you need to collect and how it will be used.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="qualities-of-a-good-questionnaire">Qualities of a Good Questionnaire<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#qualities-of-a-good-questionnaire" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A good questionnaire has the following criteria</p>
<ul>
<li>Has simple and specific questions. Avoids wording that is above the vocabulary or reading skills of the respondents.</li>
<li>Has short and precise questions. The number of questions should not be too many or else they will put off the person being interviewed. In other words, keep it short and simple (KISS).</li>
<li>Avoids use of abbreviations or jargon.</li>
<li>Avoids questions that are too demanding and time consuming.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Avoids bias in questions. Biased questions influence people to answer in a way that does not accurately reflect their position. For example, a question like Do you agree with the majority of the people that health standards are falling? implies that the respondent should agree.</li>
<li>Avoids making assumptions. Questions such as How many children do you have? assume that the respondent has children. You should only ask this question after establishing the situation with the question Do you have children?</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE
Training for Better Health
ISO 9001:2015 Certified by
UKAS 001</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">Cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Avoids double questions. For example, 'Did the MCH talk help to identify ways to improve the sanitation and nutrition of your children?' It is better to ask about sanitation and nutrition separately</li>
<li>Has clear wording. Words such as majority, older people, regularly, might mean different things to different people and so should be avoided.</li>
<li>Questions ask about simple common happenings.</li>
<li>Questions range from known to unknown and from simple to complex</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>All the questions should relate to the purpose of study. Eliminate 'nice to know' questions, you may end up with 'information overload'.</li>
<li>Questions are acceptable to the people included in the survey. You should view the questions through the respondents eye and ask yourself the following:</li>
<li>Will the question be seen as reasonable?</li>
<li>Will it infringe on the respondents privacy?</li>
<li>Will the respondent be able and willing to answer the question?</li>
<li>Questions should not screen disease if no effective treatment can be offered for the cases found or if the condition is rare.</li>
<li>Type of question should either be open- or closed-ended.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="kenya-medical-training-college">KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kenya-medical-training-college" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Questionnaire must be pre-tested before executing the survey. This helps to identify and eliminate questions that are defective or may lead to wrong information. You may even need to rephrase the questionnaire so that it can elicit the correct responses</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-information">Types of Information<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-information" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Questionnaires can help you collect four different types of information.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-understanding">1. Understanding<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-understanding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Information about what people know or how well they understand something, that is, knowledge. For example, what is the major cause of accidental deaths among children in the home?</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-beliefs-attitudes-and-opinions">2. Beliefs, Attitudes and Opinions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-beliefs-attitudes-and-opinions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Information about people's beliefs, attitudes and opinions. Here you would be asking people to share with you their thoughts, feelings, ideas, judgment or their way of thinking. For example, in your opinion does positive self-esteem prevent drug abuse among adolescents?</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</strong></p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-behaviour">5. Behaviour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-behaviour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Information about people's behaviour. That is, what people have done in the past, present, and what they plan to do in the future. For example, have you ever attended an antenatal clinic?</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-attributes">4. Attributes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-attributes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Information about peoples attributes. That is, their personal or demographic characteristics. For example, age, education, occupation and income.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-question">Types of Question<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-question" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A questionnaire should be laid out in such a way that it provides easy flow from one topic to another. It should have both open- and closed-ended</li>
<li>An open-ended question is a type of question that allows the respondent to provide their own answer. It encourages the respondent to think and describe a situation in their own words. The respondent is not given any answers to select from. The answer given is best recorded in the respondent's own words</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Although it is the easiest way to ask for information the responses are not easy to analyse. The answers are bound to be varied and so you need to categorise and summarise them.</li>
<li>Open-ended questions are useful because they give more information on:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Facts and details which the researcher may not be familiar with</li>
<li>Opinions, attitudes and suggestions</li>
<li>Sensitive issues</li>
</ol>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The following are examples of open-ended questions:</p>
<ul>
<li>What did the traditional birth attendants do when your labour started?</li>
<li>What do you think are the reasons for the high dropout rate of health committee members?</li>
<li>What would you do if you noticed that your daughter (a schoolgirl) has a relationship with her teacher?</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="closed-ended-question">Closed-ended Question<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#closed-ended-question" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>These are questions that offer the respondents a list of possible answers to choose from.</li>
<li>They are specific and useful when you are interested in certain aspects of an issue.</li>
<li>Although they produce more uniform answers than open-ended questions, they depend upon our knowing and including all the relevant answers in the list.</li>
</ul>
<p>KENYA MEDICAL TRAINING COLLEGE</p>
<p>Training for Better Health</p>
<p>ISO 9001:2015 Certified by</p>
<p>NCCERG</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">cont<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Did you eat any of the following foods yesterday? Circle 'Yes' if you ate any of the foods listed.</li>
<li>

</ol>
